aria-label="reference 39">(39)</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">SnS</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">in situ hot bath route</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">1100</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">200</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">91.8</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.014</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">Cu<sub>2</sub>S</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">molten salt electrolysis</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">5.0</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">317</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">5000</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">88.2</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.0024</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">this work</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">To illuminate the superior properties of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrode, the synergistic effect of micron-sized Cu<sub>2</sub>S flakes evolution during sodiation/desodiation and high-ionic-conductivity DME-based electrolyte were investigated. First, the phase structure and morphologies of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrodes at different cycles were detected on XRD patterns and SEM images to investigate the evolution process of Cu<sub>2</sub>S flakes. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a exhibits the comparison of XRD patterns of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrodes after 25 and 100 cycles. The sharp peaks at 45.8 and 48.5°, corresponding to (2 13 1) and (2 14 0) planes of Cu<sub>2</sub>S, gradually weaken and broaden or even disappear for some peaks after 25 and 100 cycles, which reveals the gradual refining process of the Cu<sub>2</sub>S flakes during charge and discharge. The verdict is vividly demonstrated in the morphology analysis shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b–f. The micron-sized Cu<sub>2</sub>S flakes with a smooth surface can be detected clearly in the pristine electrode, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b, whereas the flakes become smaller and the surface becomes rough after 25 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>c). After 100 cycles, a porous integrity structure, evolved from the Cu<sub>2</sub>S flakes during sodiation and desodiation, results, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>d,e. Moreover, the porous structure is still integrated even after 1000 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>f), which reveals the robustness of the porous structure in situ formed during sodiation and desodiation. The aforesaid evolution mechanism is demonstrated in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="Scheme 1">Scheme </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="1">1</a>. During the sodiation process of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrodes, homodisperse Cu and Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>S particles were formed, which is helpful to forming a Cu<sub>2</sub>S porous structure when Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>S is depleted in the desodiation process. Considering the good conductivity of Cu<sub>2</sub>S, the porous structure not only provides transmission channels and porosity for Na<sup>+</sup> and electrolyte, but also itself can be used as a good conductive network for electrons. Besides, to compare with DME-based electrolyte, the electrochemical performance of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrodes is also investigated in ethylene carbonate (EC)/diethyl carbonate (DEC)-based electrolyte, which delivers 647 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> of initial capacity but radically fades to 83 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> within 10 cycles, with only 55.6% initial Coulombic efficiency (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/suppl_file/am7b19138_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10</a>, Supporting Information). Impedance experiments of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrodes in DME- and EC/DEC-based electrolytes were conducted (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/suppl_file/am7b19138_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S11 and S12</a>) to compare interface states of the electrodes. The smaller interface impedance in DME-based electrolyte reveals the higher ion conductivity of the DME-based electrolyte and faster electrochemical process than that in the EC/DEC-based electrolyte. In short, the robust porous structure in situ formed during the charge and discharge processes and synergy with DME-based electrolyte endow Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrodes with excellent cycle performance as well as superior rate capability.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/asset/images/medium/am-2017-19138x_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/asset/images/large/am-2017-19138x_0003.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. XRD patterns (a) and SEM images of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrodes after different cycles: pristine (b), after 25 cycles (c), after 100 cycles (d, e), and after 1000 cycles (f).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/asset/images/large/am-2017-19138x_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b19138&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure id="sch1" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Scheme 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/asset/images/medium/am-2017-19138x_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/asset/images/large/am-2017-19138x_0006.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><div class="title2">Scheme 1. Schematic Illustration of Morphologies Evolution of Cu<sub>2</sub>S Electrodes at Different Cycles</div></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b19138/asset/images/large/am-2017-19138x_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b19138&amp;id=sch1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i12">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, for the first time, using Cu pellets as anode, a series of copper sulfides (Cu<sub>2</sub>S, Cu<sub>7</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and Cu<sub>7</sub>KS<sub>4</sub>) were controllably synthesized via electrochemical route in KCl–NaCl–Na<sub>2</sub>S molten salts. The as-prepared products were investigated as anode of SIBs, especially, Cu<sub>2</sub>S with micron-sized flakes structure delivers a high Na-storage capacity of 430 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 84.9%, at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Even at 20 A g<sup>–1</sup> (corresponding to 50 C), 337 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (80.2% of initial capacity) can be obtained. The excellent rate capability of Cu<sub>2</sub>S microflakes is attributed to pseudocapacitance contribution during the sodiation and desodiation processes. After 5000 cycles, a capacity retention of 88.2% is achieved at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, corresponding to 0.0024% of fade rate per cycle. The ultrahigh cycle stability of Cu<sub>2</sub>S electrode is benefited from the synergic effect of robust porous structure formed during cycled and high-ionic-conductivity DME-based electrolyte. The as-prepared Cu<sub>2</sub>S demonstrates as promising anode materials for SIBs with superior rate capability and excellent cycle performance, and the electrochemical synthesis route is extendable for the preparation of functional materials.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i13">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.7b19138" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.7b19138</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Physical and electrochemical characterization of products (C<sub>7</sub>KS<sub>4</sub>, Cu<sub>7</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and Cu<sub>2</sub>S) from 1.0, 0.8, and 0.4 V; ex situ XRD patterns of Cu<sub>2</sub>S anodes at different charge–discharge states; voltage curves of Cu<sub>2</sub>S anode at different current densities; rate capabilities comparison of different metal chalcogenide materials as SIB anodes;         </div><div class="casAbstract">With the ongoing global effort to reduce greenhouse gas emission and dependence on oil, elec. energy storage (EES) devices such as Li-ion batteries and supercapacitors have become ubiquitous.  Today, EES devices are entering the broader energy use arena and playing key roles in energy storage, transfer, and delivery within, for example, elec. vehicles, large-scale grid storage, and sensors located in harsh environmental conditions, where performance at temps. greater than 25 °C are required.  The safety and high temp. durability are as crit. or more so than other essential characteristics (e.g., capacity, energy and power d.) for safe power output and long lifespan.  Consequently, significant efforts are underway to design, fabricate, and evaluate EES devices along with characterization of device performance limitations such as thermal runaway and aging.  Energy storage under extreme conditions is limited by the material properties of electrolytes, electrodes, and their synergetic interactions, and thus significant opportunities exist for chem. advancements and technol. improvements.  In this review, we present a comprehensive anal. of different applications assocd. with high temp. use (40-200 °C), recent advances in the development of reformulated or novel materials (including ionic liqs., solid polymer electrolytes, ceramics, and Si, LiFePO4, and LiMn2O4 electrodes) with high thermal stability, and their demonstrative use in EES devices.  Finally, we present a crit. overview of the limitations of current high temp. systems and evaluate the future outlook of high temp. batteries with well-controlled safety, high energy/power d., and operation over a wide temp. range.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C6CS00776G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research development on sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                 10.1021/cr500192f</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D114%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D11636-11682%26journal%3DChem.%2BRev.%26author%3DN.%2BYabuuchi%26author%3DK.%2BKubota%26author%3DM.%2BDahbi%26author%3DS.%2BKomaba%26title%3DResearch%2Bdevelopment%2Bon%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fcr500192f&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b19138&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fcr500192f&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Kubota, Kei; Dahbi, Mouad; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">114</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11636-11682</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHREAY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0009-2665</span>.

                        cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium vanadium titanium phosphate electrode for symmetric sodium-ion batteries with high power and long lifespan</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Dongxue; Bie, Xiaofei; Fu, Qiang; Dixon, Ditty; Bramnik, Natalia; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Fauth, Francois; Wei, Yingjin; Ehrenberg, Helmut; Chen, Gang; Du, Fei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15888</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries operating at ambient temp. hold great promise for use in grid energy storage owing to their significant cost advantages.  However, challenges remain in the development of suitable electrode materials to enable long lifespan and high rate capability.  Here we report a sodium super-ionic conductor structured electrode, sodium vanadium titanium phosphate, which delivers a high specific capacity of 147 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1 C and excellent capacity retentions at high rates.  A sym. sodium-ion full cell demonstrates a superior rate capability with a specific capacity of about 49 mA h g-1 at 20 C rate and ultralong lifetime over 10,000 cycles.  Furthermore, in situ synchrotron diffraction and X-ray absorption spectroscopy measurement are carried out to unravel the underlying sodium storage mechanism and charge compensation behavior.  Our results suggest the potential application of sym. batteries for electrochem. energy storage given the superior rate capability and long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref10" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201606508"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J. B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Aqueous Symmetric Sodium-Ion Battery with NASICON-Structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub></span>. <i>Angew. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1700219</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Utilizing Co(2+)/Co(3+) Redox Couple in P2-Layered Na0.66Co0.22Mn0.44Ti0.34O2 Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Qin-Chao; Pan Yang; Xiao Na; Hong Fan; Wu Xiao-Jing; Zhou Yong-Ning; Hu Enyuan; Bak Seong-Min; Yang Xiao-Qing; Fu Zheng-Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1700219</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing sodium-ion batteries for large-scale energy storage applications is facing big challenges of the lack of high-performance cathode materials.  Here, a series of new cathode materials Na0.66Co x Mn0.66-x Ti0.34O2 for sodium-ion batteries are designed and synthesized aiming to reduce transition metal-ion ordering, charge ordering, as well as Na(+) and vacancy ordering.  An interesting structure change of Na0.66Co x Mn0.66-x Ti0.34O2 from orthorhombic to hexagonal is revealed when Co content increases from x = 0 to 0.33.  In particular, Na0.66Co0.22Mn0.44Ti0.34O2 with a P2-type layered structure delivers a reversible capacity of 120 mAh g(-1) at 0.1 C.  When the current density increases to 10 C, a reversible capacity of 63.2 mAh g(-1) can still be obtained, indicating a promising rate capability.  The low valence Co(2+) substitution results in the formation of average Mn(3.7+) valence state in Na0.66Co0.22Mn0.44Ti0.34O2, effectively suppressing the Mn(3+)-induced Jahn-Teller distortion, and in turn stabilizing the layered structure.  X-ray absorption spectroscopy results suggest that the charge compensation of Na0.66Co0.22Mn0.44Ti0.34O2 during charge/discharge is contributed by Co(2.2+)/Co(3+) and Mn(3.3+)/Mn(4+) redox couples.  This is the first time that the highly reversible Co(2+)/Co(3+) redox couple is observed in P2-layered cathodes for sodium-ion batteries.  This finding may open new approaches to design advanced intercalation-type cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref12" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1021/ja5116698"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jarry, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gottis, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>137</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3533</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3539</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja5116698</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D137%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D3533-3539%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DA.%2BJarry%26author%3DS.%2BGottis%26author%3DY.%2BS.%2BYu%26author%3DJ.%2BRoque-Rosell%26author%3DC.%2BKim%26author%3DJ.%2BCabana%26author%3DJ.%2BKerr%26author%3DR.%2BKostecki%26title%3DThe%2BFormation%2BMechanism%2Bof%2BFluorescent%2BMetal%2BComplexes%2Bat%2Bthe%2BLixNi0.5Mn1.5O4%25E2%2588%2592%25CE%25B4%252FCarbonate%2BEster%2BElectrolyte%2BInterface%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fja5116698&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b19138&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fja5116698&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Formation Mechanism of Fluorescent Metal Complexes at the LixNi0.5Mn1.5O4-δ/Carbonate Ester Electrolyte Interface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jarry, Angelique; Gottis, Sebastien; Yu, Young-Sang; Roque-Rosell, Josep; Kim, Chunjoong; Cabana, Jordi; Kerr, John; Kostecki, Robert</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">137</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3533-3539</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. oxidn. of carbonate esters at the LixNi0.5Mn1.5O4-δ/electrolyte interface results in Ni/Mn dissoln. and surface film formation, which neg. affect the electrochem. performance of Li-ion batteries.  Ex-situ X-ray absorption (XRF/XANES), Raman, and fluorescence spectroscopy, along with imaging of LixNi0.5Mn1.5O4-δ pos. and graphite neg. electrodes from tested Li-ion batteries, reveal the formation of a variety of MnII/III and NiII complexes with β-diketonate ligands.  These metal complexes, which are generated upon anodic oxidn. of Et and di-Et carbonates at LixNi0.5Mn1.5O4-δ, form a surface film that partially dissolves in the electrolyte.  The dissolved MnIII complexes are reduced to their MnII analogs, which are incorporated into the solid electrolyte interphase surface layer at the graphite neg. electrode.  This work elucidates possible reaction pathways and evaluates their implications for Li+ transport kinetics in Li-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE00695C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NaCrO2 cathode for high-rate sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Chan-Yeop; Park, Jae-Sang; Jung, Hun-Gi; Chung, Kyung-Yoon; Aurbach, Doron; Sun, Yang-Kook; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries offer a potential alternative or complementary system to lithium-ion batteries, which are widely used in many applications.  For this purpose, layered O3-type NaCrO2 for use as a cathode material in sodium-ion batteries was synthesized via an emulsion-drying method.  The produced NaCrO2 was modified using pitch as a carbon source and the products were tested in half and full cells using a NaPF6-based non-aq. electrolyte soln.  The carbon-coated NaCrO2 cathode material exhibits excellent capacity retention with superior rate capability up to a rate of 150 C (99 mA h (g oxide)-1), which corresponds to full discharge during 27 s.  The surface conducting carbon layer plays a critically important role in the excellent performance of this cathode material.  We confirmed the reaction process with sodium using X-ray diffraction and X-ray absorption spectroscopy.  Thermal anal. using time-resolved X-ray diffraction also demonstrated the structural stability of carbon-coated Na0.5CrO2.  Due to the excellent performance of the cathode material described herein, this study has the potential to promote the accelerated development of sodium-ion batteries for a large no. of applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE01876E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anomalous Jahn-Teller behavior in a manganese-based mixed-phosphate cathode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyungsub; Yoon, Gabin; Park, Inchul; Park, Kyu-Young; Lee, Byungju; Kim, Jongsoon; Park, Young-Uk; Jung, Sung-Kyun; Lim, Hee-Dae; Ahn, Docheon; Lee, Seongsu; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3325-3335</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a 3.8 V manganese-based mixed-phosphate cathode material for applications in sodium rechargeable batteries; i.e., Na4Mn3(PO4)2(P2O7).  This material exhibits a largest Mn2+/Mn3+ redox potential of 3.84 V vs.  Na+/Na yet reported for a manganese-based cathode, together with the largest energy d. of 416 W h kg-1.  We describe first-principles calcns. and exptl. results which show that three-dimensional Na diffusion pathways with low-activation-energy barriers enable the rapid sodium insertion and extn. at various states of charge of the Na4-xMn3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode (where x = 0, 1, 3).  Furthermore, we show that the sodium ion mobility in this crystal structure is not decreased by the structural changes induced by Jahn-Teller distortion (Mn3+), in contrast to most manganese-based electrodes, rather it is increased due to distortion, which opens up sodium diffusion channels.  This feature stabilizes the material, providing high cycle stability and high power performance for sodium rechargeable batteries.  The high voltage, large energy d., cycle stability and the use of low-cost Mn give Na4Mn3(PO4)2(P2O7) significant potential for applications as a cathode material for large-scale Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA03197D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qing, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Metal-organic Frameworks as Superior Cathodes for Rechargeable Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In response to the ever-increasing demand for grid-scale energy storage systems, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) working at ambient- or room-temp. are gaining much attention as promising alternatives because of the abundance and low cost of sodium resources.  However, their adoption is significantly hampered by several issues, esp. in terms of sluggish kinetics and capacity retention during cycling.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ion-Catalyzed Synthesis of Microporous Hard Carbon Embedded with Expanded Nanographite for Enhanced Lithium/Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Zhi-Long; Xin, Sen; You, Ya; Yu, Le; Lin, Yue; Xu, Da-Wei; Qiao, Chan; Huang, Zhi-Hong; Yang, Ning; Yu, Shu-Hong; Goodenough, John B.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons attract myriad interest as anode materials for high-energy rechargeable batteries due to their low costs and high theor. capacities; practically, they deliver unsatisfactory performance due to their intrinsically disordered microarchitecture.  Here a facile ion-catalyzed synthesis is reported of a phenol-formaldehyde resin-based hard-carbon aerogel that takes advantage of the chelation effect of phenol and Fe3+, which consists of a three-dimensionally interconnected carbon network embedded with hydrogen-rich, ordered microstructures of expanded nanographites and carbon micropores.  The chelation effect ensures the homodispersion of Fe in the polymer segments of the precursor, so that an effective catalytic conversion from sp3 to sp2 carbon occurs, enabling free rearrangement of graphene sheets into expanded nanographite and carbon micropores.  The structural merits of the carbon offer chances to achieve lithium/sodium storage performance far beyond that possible with the conventional carbon anode materials, including graphite and mesocarbon microbeads, along with fast kinetics and long cycle life.  In this way, the hard carbon proves its feasibility to serve as an advanced anode material for high-energy rechargeable Li/Na batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201602894"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bommier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chong, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Surta, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Neuefeind, J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional SnO Anodes with a Tunable Number of Atomic Layers for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Fan; Zhu, Jiajie; Zhang, Daliang; Schwingenschlogl, Udo; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1302-1311</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have systematically changed the no. of at. layers stacked in 2D SnO nanosheet anodes and studied their sodium ion battery (SIB) performance.  The results indicate that as the no. of at. SnO layers in a sheet decreases, both the capacity and cycling stability of the Na ion battery improve.  The thinnest SnO nanosheet anodes (two to six SnO monolayers) exhibited the best performance.  Specifically, an initial discharge and charge capacity of 1072 and 848 mAh g-1 were obsd., resp., at 0.1 A g-1.  In addn., an impressive reversible capacity of 665 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 and 452 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at a high c.d. of 1.0 A g-1 was obsd., with excellent rate performance.  As the av. no. of at. layers in the anode sheets increased, the battery performance degraded significantly.  For example, for the anode sheets with 10-20 at. layers, only a reversible capacity of 389 mAh g-1 could be obtained after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1.  D. functional theory calcns. coupled with exptl. results were used to elucidate the sodiation mechanism of the SnO nanosheets.  This systematic study of monolayer-dependent phys. and electrochem. properties of 2D anodes shows a promising pathway to engineering and mitigating vol. changes in 2D anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  It also demonstrates that ultrathin SnO nanosheets are promising SIB anode materials with high specific capacity, stable cyclability, and excellent rate performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201700129"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multichannel Porous TiO<sub>2</sub> Hollow Nanofbers with Rich Oxygen Vacancies and High Grain Boundary Density Enabling Superior Sodium Storage Performance</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1700129</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite their large theor. storage capability, Na-Sn batteries exhibit poor round-trip energy efficiencies as compared to Li-Si batteries.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-pot chemical route for morphology-controllable fabrication of Sn-Sb micro/nano-structures: Advanced anode materials for lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Zheng; Han, Qigang; Geng, Di; Wu, Yaoming; Cheng, Yong; Wang, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A series of morphol./component-controllable Sn-Sb micro/nano-structures are fabricated by a one-pot replacement reaction technique employing metallic Sn as both template and reducing agent.  Typically, nanoscaled Sn as template and Et alc. as solvent give the hollow structure, while micron-sized Sn as precursor and ethylene glycol as solvent produce the dendritic product.  Other mixed structures are also obtained by this one-pot route.  As anode materials for lithium-ion batteries, the hollow or dendritic Sn-Sb materials exhibit higher discharge capacities compared with the corresponding Sb samples as well as the Sn templates.  Esp., for the Sn-Sb hollow spheres, a high discharge capacity of 820.7 mAh g-1 after first cycle and a reversible capacity of 751 mAh g-1 are achieved after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), a potential alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIBs), have attracted remarkable attention recently due to the natural abundance and low-cost of sodium. The surface-dominated redox reaction rendered by our tailored ultrathin tin(II) sulfide nanostructures may also work in other layered materials for high-performance sodium-ion storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b05229"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Madhavi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-Dimensional Tin Disulfide Nanosheets for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">11371</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11381</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Tin Disulfide Nanosheets for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Wenping; Rui, Xianhong; Yang, Dan; Sun, Ziqi; Li, Bing; Zhang, Wenyu; Zong, Yun; Madhavi, Srinivasan; Dou, Shixue; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as complementary alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for grid energy storage due to the abundance of sodium.  However, low capacity, poor rate capability, and cycling stability of existing anodes significantly hinder the practical applications of SIBs.  Herein, ultrathin two-dimensional SnS2 nanosheets (3-4 nm in thickness) are synthesized via a facile refluxing process toward enhanced sodium storage.  The SnS2 nanosheets exhibit a high apparent diffusion coeff. of Na+ and fast sodiation/desodiation reaction kinetics.  In half-cells, the nanosheets deliver a high reversible capacity of 733 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, which still remains up to 435 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1.  The cell has a high capacity retention of 647 mA h g-1 during the 50th cycle at 0.1 A g-1, which is by far the best for SnS2, suggesting that nanosheet morphol. is beneficial to improve cycling stability in addn. to rate capability.  The SnS2 nanosheets also show encouraging performance in a full cell with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode.  In addn., the sodium storage mechanism is investigated by ex situ XRD coupled with high-resoln. TEM.  The high specific capacity, good rate capability, and cycling durability suggest that SnS2 nanosheets have great potential working as anodes for high-performance SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1039/C6RA04941A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered SnS<sub>2</sub> cross-linked by carbon nanotubes as a high performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">35197</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">35202</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Template-free synthesis of Sb2S3 hollow microspheres as anode materials for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Jianjun; Liu, Li; Xia, Jing; Zhang, Yue; Li, Min; Ouyang, Yan; Nie, Su; Wang, Xianyou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-Micro Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical Sb2S3 hollow microspheres assembled by nanowires have been successfully synthesized by a simple and practical hydrothermal reaction.  The possible formation process of this architecture was investigated by X-ray diffraction, focused-ion beam-SEM dual-beam system, and transmission electron microscopy.  When used as the anode material for lithium-ion batteries, Sb2S3 hollow microspheres manifest excellent rate property and enhanced lithium-storage capability and can deliver a discharge capacity of 674 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 after 50 cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 5000 mA g-1, a discharge capacity of 541 mAh g-1 is achieved.  Sb2S3 hollow microspheres also display a prominent sodium-storage capacity and maintain a reversible discharge capacity of 384 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 after 50 cycles.  The remarkable lithium/sodium-storage property may be attributed to the synergetic effect of its nanometer size and three-dimensional hierarchical architecture, and the outstanding stability property is attributed to the sufficient interior void space, which can buffer the vol. expansion.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref39" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700180"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kumar, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi0.94Sb1.06S3 solid soln. anode with a nanorod cluster morphol. was synthesized by a hydrothermal reaction and studied in Na-ion batteries in comparison to the binary counterparts Bi2S3 and Sb2S3.  The Bi0.94Sb1.06S3-graphite composite obtained by a mech. milling of 80% Bi0.94Sb1.06S3 and 20% graphite exhibits much improved cycle stability with 79% capacity retention after 200 cycles in the full voltage window of 0.01-2.8 V compared to its Bi2S3-graphite (58% retention) and Sb2S3-graphite (10% retention) counterparts, demonstrating a synergistic effect.  Cyclic voltammetry scans indicate that the polarization overpotential assocd. with the conversion reaction in Bi0.94Sb1.06S3 is lower than those in Sb2S3 and Bi2S3.  Cycling under controlled voltage windows of 2.8-0.85 V corresponding to a conversion reaction and 0.85-0.01 V corresponding to an alloying reaction reveals both highly reversible conversion and alloying reactions in the Bi0.94Sb1.06S3 solid soln. anode compared to that in the binary counterpart anodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201702116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrathin MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets@Metal Organic Framework Derived N-Doped Carbon Nanowall Arrays as Sodium Ion Battery Anode with Superior Cycling Life and Rate Capability</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Liquid Phase Exfoliated MoS2 Nanosheets Percolated with Carbon Nanotubes for High Volumetric/Areal Capacity Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuping; He, Xiaoyun; Hanlon, Damien; Harvey, Andrew; Coleman, Jonathan N.; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8821-8828</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The search for high-capacity, low-cost electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries is a significant challenge in energy research.  Among the many potential candidates, layered compds. such as MoS2 have attracted increasing attention.  However, such materials have not yet fulfilled their true potential.  Here, we show that networks of liq. phase exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets, reinforced with 20 wt % single-wall carbon nanotubes (SWNTs), can be formed into sodium-ion battery electrodes with large gravimetric, volumetric, and areal capacity.  The MoS2/SWNT composite films are highly porous, elec. conductive, and mech. robust due to its percolating carbon nanotube network.  When directly employed as the working electrode, they exhibit a specific capacity of &gt;400 mAh/g and volumetric capacity of ∼650 mAh/cm3.  Their mech. stability allows them to be processed into free-standing films with tunable thickness up to ∼100 μm, corresponding to an areal loading of 15 mg/cm2.  Their high elec. cond. allows the high volumetric capacity to be retained, even at high thickness, resulting in state-of-the-art areal capacities of &gt;4.0 mAh/cm2.  Such values are competitive with their lithium-ion counterparts.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201603812"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yousaf, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, R.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering Hierarchical Hollow Nickel Sulfide Spheres for High-Performance Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Dan; Sun, Wenping; Zhang, Yu; Dou, Yuhai; Jiang, Yinzhu; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for energy storage due to the abundance of sodium, esp. for grid distribution systems.  The practical implementation of SIBs, however, is severely hindered by their low energy d. and poor cycling stability due to the poor electrochem. performance of the existing electrodes.  Here, to achieve high-capacity and durable sodium storage with good rate capability, hierarchical hollow NiS spheres with porous shells composed of nanoparticles are designed and synthesized by tuning the reaction parameters.  The formation mechanism of this unique structure is systematically investigated, which is clearly revealed to be Ostwald ripening mechanism on the basis of the time-dependent morphol. evolution.  The hierarchical hollow structure provides sufficient electrode/electrolyte contact, shortened Na+ diffusion pathways, and high strain-tolerance capability.  The hollow NiS spheres deliver high reversible capacity (683.8 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate capability (337.4 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), and good cycling stability (499.9 mAh g-1 with 73% retention after 50 cycles at 0.1 A g-1).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1039/C7EE01100H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Pyrite (FeS2) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 894 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading caused by the large vol. expansion upon sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at nanoscale and applying a higher cut-off voltage are essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile etching method coupled with a novel sulfidation-in-nanobox strategy is developed to synthesize unique FeS2@C yolk-shell nanoboxes.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref51" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1021/nl801817d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wadia, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sadtler, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alivisatos, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis and Photovoltaic Application of Copper(I) Sulfide Nanocrystals</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2008</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2551</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2555</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Electrochemical Generation of Mesostructured Cu2S/C Composite for Enhanced Lithium Storage: Mechanism and Material Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Fei; Li, Wen-Cui; Li, Duo; Lu, An-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">An effective strategy is explored for the in situ generation of a Cu2S/tubular mesoporous carbon composite by exploiting the charge-discharge processes of a S/C composite on a copper-foil current collector.  By studying the reaction mechanism, we discover that the dissolved polysulfide ions (from the reaction of pristine sulfur) and inserted Li+ are firmly anchored by the copper ions released from the copper foil, which forms insol. CuxS intermediates in the mesopore channels of the carbon matrix.  Moreover, the new electrochem. active CuxS intermediates are gradually converted to the final product, Cu2S, during subsequent cycles.  The as-prepd. Cu2S nanoparticles are highly dispersed throughout the tubular mesoporous carbon, and the Cu2S/C composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 270 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C over 300 cycles, with the negligible capacity loss, when used as a cathode material for a lithium-ion battery.  Furthermore, the composite shows an outstanding rate capability with a reversible capacity of 225 mAh g-1 under a high rate of 10 C.  This work provides a convenient platform for the controlled synthesis of metal sulfides for lithium-storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref54" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.12.058"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kalimuldina, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Taniguchi, I.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High performance stoichiometric Cu<sub>2</sub>S cathode on carbon fiber current collector for lithium batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim. Const.-voltage 2.7-2.8 V electrolysis, with a graphite anode, was performed in molten CaCl2 at 950°.  After electrolysis, the pellets were removed from the molten salt and rinsed in water.  SEM, energy-dispersive x-ray anal., and fusion elemental anal. all confirmed that, when electrolyzed for &gt;4 h, the Cr2O3 pellets were fully reduced to Cr metal.  The oxygen content in the product depended on electrolysis time.  Typically, for a 6-h electrolysis, &lt;0.2 wt.% oxygen was found in the product, with the current efficiency and energy consumption being 75% and 5 kW-h/kg, resp.  The fully reduced pellets had a friable strength and could be manually crushed into a powder composed of cubic crystallites, uniform in size, that grew with the electrolysis time ≤50 μm in 15 h.  The unique product morphol. of cubic crystallites differs drastically from the nodular morphol. obsd. in other metals prepd. by similar methods and is rarely seen among various com. metal powders. High rate and long term tests indicated the excellent cycle performance due to the formation of a 3D porous electrode structure during the long term charge/discharge processes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref60" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.12.085"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Electrochemical Synthesis of LiNbO<sub>2</sub> in Molten Salts and its Application for Lithium Ion Batteries with High Rate Capability</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Electrochemical Synthesis of LiNbO2 in Molten Salts and its Application for Lithium Ion Batteries with High Rate Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei; Hu, Chen; Zhou, Min; Wang, Kangli; Li, Haomiao; Cheng, Shijie; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, the authors report an effective, fast and controllable electrochem. synthesis of layered structure LiNbO2 by electrolysis of solid Nb2O5 in molten LiF-LiCl salt.  For the 1st time, the electrochem. performance of LiNbO2 as an anode for Li ion battery was studied.  Such a material shows a high reversible capacity of ∼190 mAh g-1 at 0.25 C (1C = 200 mA g-1), superior rate capability (52 mA h g-1 at 80C) and excellent long-term cycle stability (75 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at 50C), due to the favorable kinetics benefiting from the high electronic cond. and fast Li diffusion in layered crystal structure of LiNbO2.  LiNbO2 is a promising anode candidate.  Also, this work may provide a facile and controllable way to synthesize electrode materials for Li ion batteries and other electrochem. energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref61" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms12584"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sadoway, D.                         cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolysis of a molten semiconductor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Huayi; Chung, Brice; Sadoway, Donald R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metals cannot be extd. by electrolysis of transition-metal sulfides because as liqs. they are semiconductors, which exhibit high levels of electronic conduction and metal dissoln.  Herein by introduction of a distinct secondary electrolyte, we reveal a high-throughput electro-desulfurization process that directly converts semiconducting molten stibnite (Sb2S3) into pure (99.9%) liq. antimony and sulfur vapor.  At the bottom of the cell liq. antimony pools beneath cathodically polarized molten stibnite.  At the top of the cell sulfur issues from a carbon anode immersed in an immiscible secondary molten salt electrolyte disposed above molten stibnite, thereby blocking electronic shorting across the cell.  As opposed to conventional extn. practices, direct sulfide electrolysis completely avoids generation of problematic fugitive emissions (CO2, CO and SO2), significantly reduces energy consumption, increases productivity in a single-step process (lower capital and operating costs) and is broadly applicable to a host of electronically conductive transition-metal chalcogenides.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref62" class="refNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit62" data-doi="10.1143/JJAP.12.1130"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Okamoto, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kawai, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrical Conduction and Phase Transition of Copper Sulfides</span>. <i>Jpn. Cu1·8S (digenite) and Cu1·96S (djurleite) undergo phase transitions at 90° and at 93° resp.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref67" class="refNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit67" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sim, G.                             cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref68"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref68" class="refNumLink">68</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit68" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201604532"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Urchinlike ZnS Microspheres Decorated with Nitrogen-Doped Carbon: A Superior Anode Material for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Chem. – Eur. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>23</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">157</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">166</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/chem.201604532</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D23%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D157-166%26journal%3DChem.%2B%25E2%2580%2593%2BEur.%2BJ.%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BFu%26author%3DX.%2BShi%26author%3DZ.%2BXu%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26title%3DUrchinlike%2BZnS%2BMicrospheres%2BDecorated%2Bwith%2BNitrogen-Doped%2BCarbon%253A%2BA%2BSuperior%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fchem.201604532&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b19138&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fchem.201604532&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit68R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">68</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchinlike ZnS Microspheres Decorated with Nitrogen-Doped Carbon: A Superior Anode Material for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Junming; Fu, Yun; Shi, Xiaodong; Xu, Zhenming; Zhang, Zhian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">157-166</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0947-6539</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Urchinlike ZnS microspheres decorated with nitrogen-doped carbon (ZnS@NC) were fabricated by a facile two-step method in which urchinlike ZnS microspheres were coated with polydopamine and then calcined in an inert gas atm.  When employed as the anode material for lithium-ion batteries and sodium ion batteries, ZnS@NC exhibits a reversible lithium-storage capacity of 690 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1 and a reversible sodium-storage capacity of 460 mAh g-1 after 80 cycles at 200 mA g-1.  The ZnS@NC electrode shows a high reversible lithium-storage capacity of 520 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles and a high reversible sodium-storage capacity of 380 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles even at a c.d. of 1 A g-1.  The superior electrochem. performance could be ascribed to structural merits of the urchinlike ZnS microspheres and synergistic effects between ZnS and polydopamine-derived nitrogen-doped carbon.  The lithium- and sodium-storage capacities of urchinlike ZnS@NC microspheres are in the top rank in comparison with those reported in other studies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref69"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref69" class="refNumLink">69</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit69" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b05653"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhancing sodium ion battery performance by strongly binding nanostructured Sb2S3 on sulfur-doped graphene sheets</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">10953</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">10959</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.6b05653</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D10953-10959%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DX.%2BXiong%26author%3DG.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BLin%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BOu%26author%3DF.%2BZheng%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DM.%2BLiu%26title%3DEnhancing%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbattery%2Bperformance%2Bby%2Bstrongly%2Bbinding%2Bnanostructured%2BSb2S3%2Bon%2Bsulfur-doped%2Bgraphene%2Bsheets%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.6b05653&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b19138&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.6b05653&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit69R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">69</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhancing Sodium Ion Battery Performance by Strongly Binding Nanostructured Sb2S3 on Sulfur-Doped Graphene Sheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Xunhui; Wang, Guanhua; Lin, Yuwei; Wang, Ying; Ou, Xing; Zheng, Fenghua; Yang, Chenghao; Wang, Jeng-Han; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10953-10959</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered a promising alternative to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage.  However, their inferior electrochem. performances, esp. cyclability, become the major challenge for further development of SIBs.  Large vol. change and sluggish diffusion kinetics are generally considered to be responsible for the fast capacity degrdn.  We report the strong chem. bonding of nanostructured Sb2S3 on S-doped graphene sheets (Sb2S3/SGS) that enables a stable capacity retention of 83% for 900 cycles with high capacities and excellent rate performances.  To the best of our knowledge, the cycling performance of the Sb2S3/SGS composite is superior to those reported for any other Sb-based materials for SIBs.  Computational calcns. demonstrate that S-doped graphene (SGS) has a stronger affinity for Sb2S3 and the discharge products than pure graphene, resulting in a robust composite architecture for outstanding cycling stability.  Our study shows a feasible and effective way to solve the long-term cycling stability issue for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref70"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref70" class="refNumLink">70</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit70" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201606242"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A New rGO-Overcoated Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub> Nanorods Anode for Na<sup>+</sup> Battery: In Situ X-Ray Diffraction Study on a Live Sodiation/Desodiation Process</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1606242</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201606242</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26publication_year%3D2017%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DX.%2BOu%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BXiong%26author%3DF.%2BZheng%26author%3DQ.%2BPan%26author%3DC.%2BJin%26author%3DM.%2BLiu%26author%3DK.%2BHuang%26title%3DA%2BNew%2BrGO-Overcoated%2BSb2Se3%2BNanorods%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BNa%252B%2BBattery%253A%2BIn%2BSitu%2BX-Ray%2BDiffraction%2BStudy%2Bon%2Ba%2BLive%2BSodiation%252FDesodiation%2BProcess%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201606242&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b19138&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201606242&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
